==Latin==

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|adolēscō}}

===Etymology 1===
From {{affix|la|ad-|olēscō}}.

====Verb====
{{la-verb|adolēscō|adolēscere|adolēvī|perf2=adoluī|adultum|conj=3|pattern=nopass}}

# I [[grow up]]
# I [[mature]]
# I [[increase]] or [[augment]]

=====Inflection=====
* The only attested passive forms are those from {{m|la|adultus}}, which is used in an active sense.
{{la-conj-3rd|adolēsc|adolēv/adolu|adult|sync_perf=poet|type=nopass}}

===Etymology 2===
From {{affix|la|adoleō|gloss1=burn|-scō}}.

====Verb====
{{la-verb|adolēscō|adolēscere|conj=3|pattern=nopass-noperf}}

# I am [[kindled]] or [[burn]] (of a sacrifice)

=====Inflection=====
* This verb is [[defective verb|defective]], with only those forms based on the first principal part.
{{la-conj-3rd|type=nopass-noperf|adolēsc}}

===Descendants===

* {{desc|io|adolecar}}

==Latin==

===Etymology===

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|albēscō}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|albēscō|albēscere|conj=3|pattern=nopass-noperf}}

# I become [[white]], [[pale]].
# I [[gleam]].
# {{lb|la|figuratively}} I [[dawn]].

====Inflection====
* This verb is [[defective verb|defective]], with only those forms based on the first principal part.
{{la-conj-3rd|albēsc|type=nopass-noperf}}

====Synonyms====
* {{sense|become white}} {{l|la|canesco|cānēscō}}

{{la-conj-3rd|type=nopass-noperf|alēsc}}

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|convēscor}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|convēscor|convēscī|conj=3|pattern=depon-noperf}}

# I [[eat]] with (someone).
#* Bede, ''Homilia XXX'' (on the calling of Matthew)
#*: ...nec si in peccatis perseverare decernerent, ei qui sine peccato est, '''convesci''' auderent.
#*:: ...nor, if they were decided to persevere in sins, '''with''' him who is without sin would they dare to '''eat'''.

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|type=depon-noperf|convēsc}}

{{la-verb|exolēscō|exolēscere|exolēvī|exolētum|conj=3|pattern=nopass}}

# I grow out, I attain my full size, grow up
## {{lb|la|in general}} I grow up, become full-grown, I mature
## {{lb|la|in particular}} {{rfdef|lang=la}}
# {{lb|la|chiefly|ante-Augustan}} I grow to an end, I stop growing
#: {{ux|la|[[multus|Multa]] [[sum|sunt]] [[qui|quae]] [[neglegentiā]] '''exolescunt''' [[et]] [[facio|fīunt]] [[sterilis|sterilia]].|There are many that '''stop growing''' and are rendered barren by neglect.}}
## {{lb|la|transferred sense|in general}} I grow out of use, out of date, I become obsolete, I pass away, cease
##: {{ux|la|'''exolescentēs''' [[littera|litterae]]|t='''disappearing''' [''i.e.'', '''rubbed off'''] letters}}

Page 3641 patesco: -------- begin text ---------
==Latin==

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|patēscō}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|patēscō|patēscere|patuī|conj=3|pattern=nopass}}

# I am [[opening]], being [[revealed]], being [[disclosed]].
# I become [[known]]
# I [[extend]] or [[stretch]] out.

====Usage notes====
Like most inchoative verbs, {{m|la||patēscō}} is intransitive and tends to imply a change of state or ongoing action. When the state of being open has been achieved, the verb [[pateo|patēo]] is used, though the distinction is less apparent in the figurative senses. The verbs [[patefacio|patefaciō]] and [[aperio|aperiō]] are common corresponding transitive verbs which mean "to open [something]".

====Inflection====
* Note: perfect forms are shared with [[pateo|pateō]].
{{la-conj-3rd|type=nopass|patēsc|patu}}

===References===
* {{R:L&S}}
* {{R:Elementary Lewis}}
* {{R:Gaffiot}}
-------- end text --------

===Etymology===
Either:
* from {{prefix|la|per|t1=thoroughly|horrēscō|t2=tremble, dread}}; or
* from {{suffix|la|perhorreō|t1=tremble greatly|scō|pos2=inchoative}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|per.horrēscō}}

# {{lb|la|in speech}} I [[make]] a [[pause]].

==Latin==

===Etymology===
From {{prefix|la|re|quiēscō|gloss2=rest, repose}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|requiēscō}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|requiēscō|requiēscere|requiēvī|requiētum|conj=3}}

# {{lb|la|intransitive}} I [[rest]], [[repose]].
#* {{Q|la|Jerome|Vulgate|Exodus|20|11|quote=Sex enim diebus fecit Dominus caelum et terram, et mare, et omnia quae in eis sunt, et '''requievit''' in die septimo: idcirco benedixit Dominus diei sabbati, et sanctificavit eum.|trans=For in six days the LORD made heaven and earth, the sea, and all that in them is, and '''rested''' the seventh day: wherefore the LORD blessed the sabbath day, and hallowed it.}}
# {{lb|la|intransitive}} I take [[consolation]]; find [[rest]] or [[comfort]].
# {{lb|la|intransitive}} I am [[supported]] (by), rest (on).
# {{lb|la|transitive}} I let rest; [[stop]], [[stay]], [[arrest]].

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|requiēsc|requiēv|requiēt}}

====Synonyms====
* {{sense|rest}} {{l|la|acquiēscō}}, {{l|la|conquiēscō}}, {{l|la|quiēscō}}

====Derived terms====
* {{l|la|requiētiō}}
* {{l|la|requiētōrium}}
* {{l|la|requiētus}}

====Descendants====
* English: {{l|en|requiesce}}

====Related terms====
{{top2}}
* {{l|la|acquiēscō}} / {{l|la|adquiēscō}}
* {{l|la|conquiēscō}}
* {{l|la|interquiēscō}}
{{mid2}}
* {{l|la|perquiēscō}}
* {{l|la|quiēscō}}
{{bottom}}

===References===

* {{R:Elementary Lewis}}
* {{R:Gaffiot}}

==Latin==

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|serēscō}}

===Etymology 1===
From {{der|la|ine-pro|*kseros}}. Cognates include Ancient Greek {{m|grc|ξηρός}}, Old High German {{m|goh|serawēn}}, Old Armenian {{m|xcl|չոր}}, Middle Armenian {{m|axm|չիր}} and perhaps Sanskrit {{m|sa|क्षार|tr=kṣārá||sharp, acrid, pungent}}. Possibly the inchoative of an unattested verb {{m|la|*serō}}, which also produced the adjective {{m|la|serēnus}}.

====Verb====
{{la-verb|serēscō|serēscere|pattern=nopass-noperf|conj=3}}

# I become [[dry]].

=====Inflection=====
{{la-conj-3rd|type=nopass-noperf|serēsc}}

===Etymology 2===
{{affix|la|serum|t1=[[whey]]|-ēscō}}

====Verb====
{{la-verb|serēscō|serēscere|pattern=nopass-noperf|conj=3}}

# I turn into [[whey]].

=====Inflection=====
{{la-conj-3rd|type=nopass-noperf|serēsc}}

==Latin==

===Etymology===
{{PIE word|la|swé}}
{{PIE root|la|dʰeh₁}}
From {{der|la|ine-pro|*swe-dʰh₁-sk-}}, expanded from the reflexive pronoun {{der|la|ine-pro|*swé||self}} + {{m|ine-pro|*dʰeh₁-||to put, place, set}}, thus the original sense to "set as one's own". Cognate with {{m|la|soleō}}, {{m|la|sodālis}}, Ancient Greek {{m|grc|ἔθω}}, {{m|grc|εἴωθα}}, {{m|grc|ἔθνος}}, {{m|grc|ἔθος}}, {{m|grc|ἦθος}}, Sanskrit {{m|sa|स्वधा}} and Gothic {{m|got|𐍃𐌹𐌳𐌿𐍃}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|svēscō}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|suēscō|suēscere|suēvī|suētum|conj=3}}

# {{lb|la|intransitive|rare|poetic}} I become [[used]] or [[accustomed]] to
# {{lb|la|transitive|rare|post-Classical}} I [[accustom]], [[habituate]], [[train]]

===Usage notes===
This verb is rare and poetic, and prefixed forms such as {{m|la|adsuēsco}} are more frequent.

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|suēsc|suēv|suēt}}

====Derived terms====
* {{l|la|adsuēscō}}
* {{l|la|cōnsuēscō}}
* {{l|la|dēsuēscō}}
* {{l|la|mānsuēsco}}

* {{R:Gaffiot}}
* {{R:De Vaan 2008}}
